<p><b>Burkina Faso</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/En-us-Burkina_Faso.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; padding: 0 .1em;" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Burkina_Faso.ogg" title="File:En-us-Burkina Faso.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ər</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'bead'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">iː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ə</span></a></span> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˌ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'f' in 'find'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">f</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'spa'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɑː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">s</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'bode'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">oʊ</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling" class="Unicode"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Wikipedia:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>bər-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">KEE</span></span></span></b>-nə</i></a></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling" class="Unicode"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Wikipedia:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">FAH</span></span></span></b>-soh</i></a></span>; <small>French:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[buʁkina faso]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> around 274,200 square kilometres (105,900&#160;sq&#160;mi) in size. It is surrounded by six countries: <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to the east; <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a> to the southeast; <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> to the south; and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to the southwest. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>. As of 2014, its population was estimated at just over 17.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-INSD_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSD-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Formerly called the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a>, the country was <a href="/wiki/Geographical_renaming" title="Geographical renaming">renamed</a> "Burkina Faso" on 4 August 1984 by then-President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>. Residents of Burkina Faso are known as <i>Burkinabè</i> (<span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ər</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'bead'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">iː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ə</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">eɪ</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling" class="Unicode"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Wikipedia:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>bər-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">KEE</span></span></span></b>-nə-bay</i></a></span>). French is an official language of government and business.</p>
<p>Before the conquest of what is now Burkina Faso by the French and other <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial powers</a> during the late 19th century the country was ruled by various ethnic groups including the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Kingdoms" title="Mossi Kingdoms">Mossi kingdoms</a>. After gaining independence from France in 1960, the country underwent many governmental changes. Today it is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> republic. <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a> was the most recent president and ruled the country from 1987<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> until he was ousted from power by the popular youth upheaval of 31 October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Burkina_Faso" title="History of Burkina Faso">History of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The northwestern part of today's Burkina Faso was populated by <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> between 14,000 and 5000 BC. Their tools, including <a href="/wiki/Scraper_(archaeology)" title="Scraper (archaeology)">scrapers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chisel" title="Chisel">chisels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arrowhead" title="Arrowhead">arrowheads</a>, were discovered in 1973 through <a href="/wiki/Archeological" title="Archeological" class="mw-redirect">archeological</a> excavations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Agricultural" title="Agricultural" class="mw-redirect">Agricultural</a> settlements were established between 3600 and 2600 BC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bura_culture" title="Bura culture">Bura culture</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Iron_age" title="Iron age" class="mw-redirect">Iron-Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a> centered in the southwest portion of modern-day Niger and in the southeast part of contemporary Burkina Faso.<sup id="cite_ref-whc.unesco.org_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whc.unesco.org-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iron_industry" title="Iron industry" class="mw-redirect">Iron industry</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forging</a> for tools and weapons, had developed in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> by 1200 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Historians debate the exact dates when Burkina Faso's many ethnic groups arrived. The <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Proto-Mossi</a> arrived in the far eastern part of what is today Burkina Faso sometime between AD 700 and the 11th century,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Samo_language_(Burkina)" title="Samo language (Burkina)">Samo</a> arrived around the 1400s,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dogon_people" title="Dogon people">Dogon</a> lived in Burkina Faso's north and northwest regions until sometime in the 15th or 16th centuries,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and many of the other ethnic groups that make up the country's population arrived in the region during this time.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MossiCavalry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg/220px-MossiCavalry.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg/330px-MossiCavalry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="314" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MossiCavalry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The cavalry of the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Kingdoms" title="Mossi Kingdoms">Mossi Kingdoms</a> were experts at raiding deep into enemy territory, even against the formidable <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/220px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/330px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/440px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2325" data-file-height="1693" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Resistance to the French invasion at <a href="/wiki/Bobo-Dioulasso" title="Bobo-Dioulasso">Bobo-Dioulasso</a> in 1892.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> the Mossi established several separate kingdoms including those of Tenkodogo, Yatenga, Gourma, Zandoma, and Ouagadougou.<sup id="cite_ref-Nations_2014_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nations_2014-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Sometime between 1328 and 1338 Mossi warriors raided <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> but the Mossi were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Sonni_Ali" title="Sonni Ali">Sonni Ali</a> of <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai</a> at the Battle of Kobi in <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> in 1483.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the early 16th century the Songhai conducted many slave raids into what is today Burkina Faso.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 18th century the Gwiriko Empire was established at <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso" title="Bobo Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect">Bobo Dioulasso</a> and ethnic groups such as the Dyan, Lobi, and Birifor settled along the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black Volta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_colony_to_independence_.281890s.E2.80.931958.29">From colony to independence (1890s–1958)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: From colony to independence (1890s–1958)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Starting in the early 1890s a series of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> military officers made attempts to claim parts of what is today Burkina Faso. At times these <a href="/wiki/Colonialists" title="Colonialists" class="mw-redirect">colonialists</a> and their armies fought the local peoples; at times they forged alliances with them and made treaties. The colonialist officers and their home governments also made treaties amongst themselves. Through a complex series of events what is Burkina Faso eventually became a French protectorate in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The eastern and western regions, where a standoff against the forces of the powerful ruler <a href="/wiki/Samori_Ture" title="Samori Ture">Samori Ture</a> complicated the situation, came under French occupation in 1897. By 1898, the majority of the territory corresponding to Burkina Faso was nominally conquered; however, French control of many parts remained uncertain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_Convention_of_1898" title="Anglo-French Convention of 1898">Franco-British Convention of 14 June 1898</a> created the country's modern borders. In the French territory, a war of conquest against local communities and political powers continued for about five years. In 1904, the largely pacified territories of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta basin</a> were integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Senegal_and_Niger" title="Upper Senegal and Niger">Upper Senegal and Niger</a> colony of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> as part of the reorganization of the French West African colonial empire. The colony had its capital in <a href="/wiki/Bamako" title="Bamako">Bamako</a>.</p>
<p>The French imposed their own language as the official one for colonial administration and generally appointed French colonists or nationals to prominent positions. The French started some schools and selected top students for additional education in France.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">Draftees</a> from the territory participated in the European fronts of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in the battalions of the <a href="/wiki/Tirailleurs_s%C3%A9n%C3%A9galais" title="Tirailleurs sénégalais" class="mw-redirect">Senegalese Rifles</a>. Between 1915 and 1916, the districts in the western part of what is now Burkina Faso and the bordering eastern fringe of Mali became the stage of one of the most important armed oppositions to colonial government: the <a href="/wiki/Volta-Bani_War" title="Volta-Bani War">Volta-Bani War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The French government finally suppressed the movement but only after suffering defeats. It also had to organize its largest expeditionary force of its colonial history to send into the country to suppress the insurrection. Armed opposition wracked the Sahelian north when the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> and allied groups of the Dori region ended their truce with the government.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/220px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/330px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/440px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="788" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The capital, <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, in 1930</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French Upper Volta</a> was established on 1 March 1919. The French feared a recurrence of armed uprising and had related economic considerations. To bolster its administration, the colonial government separated the present territory of Burkina Faso from Upper Senegal and Niger.</p>
<p>The new colony was named <i><a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">Haute Volta</a>,</i> and François Charles Alexis Édouard Hesling became its first <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Upper_Volta" title="List of governors of Upper Volta" class="mw-redirect">governor</a>. Hesling initiated an ambitious road-making program to improve infrastructure and promoted the growth of cotton for export. The cotton policy&#160;– based on <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a>&#160;– failed, and revenue generated by the colony stagnated. The colony was dismantled on 5 September 1932, being split between the French colonies of <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Côte d'Ivoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>. Côte d'Ivoire received the largest share, which contained most of the population as well as the cities of Ouagadougou and <a href="/wiki/Bobo-Dioulasso" title="Bobo-Dioulasso">Bobo-Dioulasso</a>.</p>
<p>France reversed this change during the period of intense anti-colonial agitation that followed the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. On 4 September 1947, it revived the colony of Upper Volta, with its previous boundaries, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>. The French designated its colonies as departments of the metropole France on the European continent.</p>
<p>On 11 December 1958 the colony achieved <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-government</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a>; it joined the Franco-African Community. A revision in the organization of French Overseas Territories had begun with the passage of the Basic Law (Loi Cadre) of 23 July 1956. This act was followed by reorganization measures approved by the French parliament early in 1957 to ensure a large degree of self-government for individual territories. Upper Volta became an autonomous republic in the French community on 11 December 1958. Full independence from France was received in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Volta_.281958.E2.80.931984.29">Upper Volta (1958–1984)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Upper Volta (1958–1984)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg/220px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg/330px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg/440px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2892" data-file-height="2175" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_-_Golda_Meir_1961.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo" title="Maurice Yaméogo">Maurice Yaméogo</a> (center) was the first President of Burkina Faso.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a></div>
<p>The Republic of Upper Volta (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>République de Haute-Volta</i></span>) was established on 11 December 1958 as a <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colony</a> within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>. The name Upper Volta related to the nation's location along the upper reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta River</a>. The river's three <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> are called the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red Volta</a>. These were expressed in the three colors of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Upper_Volta" title="Flag of Upper Volta">former national flag</a>.</p>
<p>Before attaining autonomy, it had been <a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French Upper Volta</a> and part of the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>. On 5 August 1960, it attained full independence from <a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic">France</a>. The first president, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo" title="Maurice Yaméogo">Maurice Yaméogo</a>, was the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Voltaic_Democratic_Union" title="Voltaic Democratic Union" class="mw-redirect">Voltaic Democratic Union</a> (UDV). The 1960 constitution provided for election by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> of a president and a national assembly for five-year terms. Soon after coming to power, Yaméogo banned all political parties other than the UDV. The government lasted until 1966. After much unrest, including mass demonstrations and strikes by students, labor unions, and civil servants, the military intervened.</p>
<p>The military <i><a href="/wiki/1966_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1966 Upper Voltan coup d'état">coup d'état</a></i> deposed Yaméogo, suspended the constitution, dissolved the National Assembly, and placed Lt. Col. <a href="/wiki/Sangoul%C3%A9_Lamizana" title="Sangoulé Lamizana">Sangoulé Lamizana</a> at the head of a government of senior army officers. The army remained in power for four years. On 14 June 1970, the Voltans ratified a new constitution that established a four-year transition period toward complete civilian rule. Lamizana remained in power throughout the 1970s as president of military or mixed civil-military governments. After conflict over the 1970 constitution, a new constitution was written and approved in 1977. Lamizana was reelected by open elections in 1978.</p>
<p>Lamizana's government faced problems with the country's traditionally powerful trade unions, and on 25 November 1980, Col. <a href="/wiki/Saye_Zerbo" title="Saye Zerbo">Saye Zerbo</a> overthrew President Lamizana in a <a href="/wiki/1980_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Upper Voltan coup d'état">bloodless coup</a>. Colonel Zerbo established the Military Committee of Recovery for National Progress as the supreme governmental authority, thus eradicating the 1977 constitution.</p>
<p>Colonel Zerbo also encountered resistance from trade unions and was overthrown two years later, on 7 November 1982, by Maj. Dr. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Ou%C3%A9draogo" title="Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo">Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo</a> and the Council of Popular Salvation (CSP). The CSP continued to ban political parties and organizations, yet promised a transition to civilian rule and a new constitution.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1983_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat">1983 coup d'état</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1983 coup d'état">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Factional infighting developed between moderates in the CSP and the radicals, led by Capt. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>, who was appointed prime minister in January 1983. The internal political struggle and Sankara's leftist rhetoric led to his arrest and subsequent efforts to bring about his release, directed by Capt. <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a>. This release effort resulted in yet another military coup d'état on 4 August 1983.</p>
<p>The coup brought Sankara to power and his government began to implement a series of "revolutionary" programs which included mass-vaccinations, infrastructure improvements, the expansion of women's rights, encouragement of domestic agricultural consumption, and anti-desertification projects.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burkina_Faso_.281984.E2.80.93.29">Burkina Faso (1984–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Burkina Faso (1984–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 4 August 1984,<sup id="cite_ref-WDL1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> as a result of President Sankara's activities, the country's name was changed from Upper Volta to Burkina Faso (<i>land of the upright/honest people</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg/220px-Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg/330px-Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg/440px-Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg 2x" data-file-width="532" data-file-height="387" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pionniers_de_la_r%C3%A9volution.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pioneers_of_the_Revolution" title="Pioneers of the Revolution">Pioneers of the Revolution</a>, ca. 1985</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sankara's government formed the National Council for the Revolution (CNR), with Sankara as its president, and established popular <a href="/wiki/Committees_for_the_Defense_of_the_Revolution_(Burkina_Faso)" title="Committees for the Defense of the Revolution (Burkina Faso)">Committees for the Defense of the Revolution</a> (CDRs) to "mobilize the masses" and implement the CNR's revolutionary programs. The regime created a youth program (the Pioneers of the Revolution) for indoctrinating children with Marxist ideals.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The government also armed and deputized CDR members who began a campaign to weed out suspected anti-revolutionaries, causing discontent amongst the country's population and increasing domestic opposition to Sankara's regime.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sankara's "revolution" took place within the context of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, and his visits to the Soviet Union and Cuba, calls for the cancellation of African debts held by Western governments and institutions and <a href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist" class="mw-redirect">Marxist</a> political regime were controversial <small><i>[with whom?]</i></small>.</p>
<p>On 15 October 1987, Sankara along with twelve other officials were killed in a coup d'état organized by <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a>, Sankara's former colleague and Burkina Faso's president until October 2014. After the coup and although Sankara was known to be dead, some CDRs mounted an armed resistance to the army for several days.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Deterioration in relations with neighbouring countries was one of the reasons given by Compaoré for the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Compaoré argued that Sankara had jeopardised foreign relations with the former colonial power France and neighbouring Côte d'Ivoire (both of which supported the change in government<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>). Following the coup Compaoré immediately reversed the nationalizations, overturned nearly all of Sankara's policies, returned the country back into the IMF fold, and ultimately spurned most of Sankara's legacy. Limited democratic reforms were introduced in 1990 by Compaoré. Under the new constitution, Compaoré was re-elected without opposition in 1991. In 1998 Compaoré won election in a landslide. In 2004 13 people were tried for plotting a coup against President Compaoré and the coup's alleged mastermind was sentenced to life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2014, Burkina Faso remains one of the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">least developed countries</a> in the world.</p>
<p>Compaoré's government has played the role of negotiator in several West-African disputes including the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Ivorian_crisis" title="2010–11 Ivorian crisis">2010–11 Ivorian crisis</a>, the Inter-Togolese Dialogue, and the <a href="/wiki/2012_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Malian coup d'état">2012 Malian Crisis</a>.</p>
<p>Between February and April 2011, the death of a schoolboy provoked <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkinab%C3%A8_protests" title="2011 Burkinabè protests" class="mw-redirect">protests</a> throughout the country, coupled with a military mutiny and a magistrates' strike.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="October_2014_protests">October 2014 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: October 2014 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_Burkinab%C3%A9_uprising" title="2014 Burkinabé uprising">2014 Burkinabé uprising</a></div>
<p>Starting on 28 October 2014 protesters began to march and demonstrate in Ouagadougou against President <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaore" title="Blaise Compaore" class="mw-redirect">Blaise Compaore</a> who appeared ready to amend the constitution and extend his 27-year rule. On 30 October, some protesters set fire to the parliament<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> and took over the national TV headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou_Airport" title="Ouagadougou Airport">Ouagadougou International Airport</a> was closed and MPs suspended the vote on changing the constitution to allow Compaoré to stand for re-election in 2015. Later in the day, the military dissolved all government institutions and set a <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 October 2014, President Compaoré, facing mounting pressure, resigned after 27 years in office.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yacouba_Isaac_Zida" title="Yacouba Isaac Zida">Lt. Col. Isaac Zida</a> said that he will lead the country during its transitional period before the planned <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_2015" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 2015" class="mw-redirect">2015 presidential election</a> but there are concerns over his close ties to the former president.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2014 opposition parties, civil society groups and religious leaders adopted a plan for a transitional authority to guide Burkina Faso to elections.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Under the plan <a href="/wiki/Michel_Kafando" title="Michel Kafando">Michel Kafando</a> was made the transitional <a href="/wiki/President_of_Burkina_Faso" title="President of Burkina Faso" class="mw-redirect">President of Burkina Faso</a> and Lt. Col. Zida became the acting Prime Minister and Defense Minister.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/220px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/330px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/440px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png 2x" data-file-width="605" data-file-height="653" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a> ruled Burkina Faso from a coup d'état in 1987 until he lost power in 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4512" data-file-height="3384" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Burkina_Faso" title="National Assembly of Burkina Faso">National Assembly</a> building in downtown <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Politics of Burkina Faso">Politics of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>With French help, <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a> seized power in a coup d'état in 1987. He overthrew his long-time friend and ally <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>, who was killed in the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Constitution of Burkina Faso">constitution</a> of 2 June 1991 established a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential government</a>: its parliament can be dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Burkina_Faso" title="List of heads of state of Burkina Faso">President of the Republic</a>, who is <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Elections in Burkina Faso">elected</a> for a term of seven years. In 2000, the constitution was amended to reduce the presidential term to five years and set term limits to two, preventing successive re-election. The amendment took effect during the 2005 elections. If passed beforehand, it would have prevented Compaoré from being reelected.</p>
<p>Other presidential candidates challenged the election results. But in October 2005, the constitutional council ruled that, because Compaoré was the sitting president in 2000, the amendment would not apply to him until the end of his second term in office. This cleared the way for his candidacy in <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso_presidential_elections,_2005" title="Burkina Faso presidential elections, 2005" class="mw-redirect">the 2005 election</a>. On 13 November, Compaoré was reelected in a landslide, because of a divided political opposition.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_2010" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 2010">2010 Presidential elections</a>, President Compaoré was re-elected. Only 1.6 million Burkinabés voted, out of a total population 10 times that size.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkinab%C3%A8_protests" title="2011 Burkinabè protests" class="mw-redirect">2011 Burkinabè protests</a> were a series of popular protests that called for the resignation of Compaoré, democratic reforms, higher wages for troops and public servants and economic freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result Governors were replaced and wages for public servants were raised.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a> consists of <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">one chamber</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Burkina_Faso)" title="National Assembly (Burkina Faso)" class="mw-redirect">National Assembly</a> which has 111 seats with members elected to serve five-year terms. There is also a constitutional chamber, composed of ten members, and an economic and social council whose roles are purely consultative. The 1991 constitution created a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament but the upper house (Chamber of Representatives) was abolished in 2002.</p>
<p>The Compaoré administration has worked to <a href="/wiki/Decentralization#Government_decentralization" title="Decentralization">decentralize power</a> by devolving some of its powers to regions and municipal authorities. But the widespread distrust of politicians and lack of political involvement by many residents complicates this process. Critics describe this as a hybrid decentralisation.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">Political freedoms</a> are severely restricted in Burkina Faso. <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">Human rights organizations</a> have criticised the Compaoré administration for numerous acts of state-sponsored violence against journalists and other politically active members of society.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Foreign relations of Burkina Faso">Foreign relations of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>Burkina Faso is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">Community of Sahel-Saharan States</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" title="La Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">La Francophonie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Military of Burkina Faso">Military of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Army of Burkina Faso" class="mw-redirect">army</a> consists of some 6,000 men in voluntary service, augmented by a part-time national People's Militia composed of civilians between 25 and 35 years of age who are trained in both military and civil duties. According to <i>Jane’s Sentinel Country Risk Assessment</i>, Burkina Faso's Army is undermanned for its force structure and poorly equipped, but has wheeled light-armour vehicles, and may have developed useful combat expertise through interventions in Liberia and elsewhere in Africa.</p>
<p>In terms of training and equipment, the regular Army is believed to be neglected in relation to the élite Presidential Security Regiment (RSP). Reports have emerged in recent years of disputes over pay and conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> There is an air force with some 19 operational aircraft, but no navy, as the country is landlocked. Military expenses constitute approximately 1.2% of the nation’s GDP.</p>
<p>In April 2011, there was an <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkina_Faso_mutiny" title="2011 Burkina Faso mutiny" class="mw-redirect">army mutiny</a>; the president named new chiefs of staff, and a curfew was imposed in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Burkina Faso employs numerous police and security forces, generally modeled after organizations used by <a href="/wiki/French_police" title="French police" class="mw-redirect">French police</a>. France continues to provide significant support and training to police forces. The <i>Gendarmerie Nationale</i> is organized along military lines, with most police services delivered at the brigade level. The <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a> operates under the authority of the Minister of Defence, and its members are employed chiefly in the rural areas and along borders.<sup id="cite_ref-Das.2C_pp._139.E2.80.93141_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Das.2C_pp._139.E2.80.93141-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There is a municipal police force controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Territorial_Administration" title="Ministry of Territorial Administration" class="mw-redirect">Ministry of Territorial Administration</a>; a national police force controlled by the Ministry of Security; and an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Regiment_of_Presidential_Security" title="Regiment of Presidential Security">Regiment of Presidential Security</a> (<i>Régiment de la Sécurité Présidentielle</i>, or RSP), a ‘palace guard’ devoted to the protection of the President of the Republic. Both the gendarmerie and the national police are subdivided into both administrative and judicial police functions; the former are detailed to protect public order and provide security, the latter are charged with criminal investigations.<sup id="cite_ref-Das.2C_pp._139.E2.80.93141_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Das.2C_pp._139.E2.80.93141-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>All foreigners and citizens are required to carry photo ID passports, or other forms of identification or risk a fine, and police spot identity checks are commonplace for persons traveling by auto, <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">bush-taxi</a>, or bus.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_sat.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/220px-Burkina_sat.png" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/330px-Burkina_sat.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/440px-Burkina_sat.png 2x" data-file-width="950" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_sat.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite image of Burkina Faso.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Geography of Burkina Faso">Geography of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Burkina Faso lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_parallel_north" title="9th parallel north">9°</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">15°N</a> (a small area is north of 15°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">6°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/3rd_meridian_east" title="3rd meridian east">3°E</a>.</p>
<p>It is made up of two major types of countryside. The larger part of the country is covered by a <a href="/wiki/Peneplain" title="Peneplain">peneplain</a>, which forms a gently undulating landscape with, in some areas, a few isolated hills, the last vestiges of a <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">massif</a>. The southwest of the country, on the other hand, forms a <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> massif, where the highest peak, Ténakourou, is found at an elevation of 749 meters (2,457&#160;ft). The massif is bordered by sheer cliffs up to 150&#160;m (492&#160;ft) high. The average altitude of Burkina Faso is 400&#160;m (1,312&#160;ft) and the difference between the highest and lowest terrain is no greater than 600&#160;m (1,969&#160;ft). Burkina Faso is therefore a relatively flat country.</p>
<p>The country owes its former name of Upper Volta to three rivers which cross it: the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black Volta</a> (or <i>Mouhoun</i>), the <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White Volta</a> (<i>Nakambé</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red Volta</a> (<i>Nazinon</i>). The Black Volta is one of the country's only two rivers which flow year-round, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Komo%C3%A9_River" title="Komoé River">Komoé</a>, which flows to the southwest. The basin of the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a> also <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drains</a> 27% of the country's surface.</p>
<p>The Niger's <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a>&#160;– the Béli, the Gorouol, the Goudébo and the Dargol&#160;– are <a href="/wiki/Torrent_(stream)" title="Torrent (stream)" class="mw-redirect">seasonal streams</a> and flow for only four to six months a year. They still can flood and overflow, however. The country also contains numerous lakes&#160;– the principal ones are Tingrela, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Bam" title="Lake Bam">Bam</a> and Dem. The country contains large ponds, as well, such as Oursi, Béli, Yomboli and Markoye. <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">Water shortages</a> are often a problem, especially in the north of the country.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WP_35,_SDr9776.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/220px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/330px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/440px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WP_35,_SDr9776.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">Savannah</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Gbomblora_Department" title="Gbomblora Department">Gbomblora Department</a>, on the road from <a href="/wiki/Gaoua" title="Gaoua">Gaoua</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bati%C3%A9,_Burkina_Faso" title="Batié, Burkina Faso">Batié</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Regions of Burkina Faso">Regions of Burkina Faso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Provinces of Burkina Faso">Provinces of Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Departments of Burkina Faso">Departments of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>The country is divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Regions of Burkina Faso">13 administrative regions</a>. These regions encompass <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Provinces of Burkina Faso">45 provinces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Departments of Burkina Faso">301 departments</a>. Each region is administered by a <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">Governor</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Climate of Burkina Faso" class="mw-redirect">Climate of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>Burkina Faso has a primarily tropical climate with two very distinct seasons. In the rainy season, the country receives between 600 and 900&#160;mm (23.6 and 35.4&#160;in) of rainfall; in the dry season, the <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a>&#160;– a hot dry wind from the Sahara&#160;– blows. The rainy season lasts approximately four months, May/June to September, and is shorter in the north of the country. Three climatic zones can be defined: the Sahel, the Sudan-Sahel, and the Sudan-Guinea. The <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> in the north typically receives less than 600&#160;mm (23.6&#160;in)<sup id="cite_ref-relationship_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relationship-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> of rainfall per year and has high temperatures, 5–47&#160;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (41.0–116.6&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>).</p>
<p>A relatively dry <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna" title="Tropical savanna" class="mw-redirect">tropical savanna</a>, the Sahel extends beyond the borders of Burkina Faso, from the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> to the Atlantic Ocean, and borders the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> to its north and the fertile region of the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudan</a> to the South. Situated between 11°3' and 13°5' north <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>, the Sudan-Sahel region is a transitional zone with regards to rainfall and temperature. Further to the south, the Sudan-Guinea zone receives more than 900&#160;mm (35.4&#160;in)<sup id="cite_ref-relationship_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relationship-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> of rain each year and has cooler average temperatures.</p>
<p>Burkina Faso's natural resources include <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pumice" title="Pumice">pumice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_mining" title="Salt mining">salt</a> and small deposits of gold.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_and_the_environment">Wildlife and the environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Wildlife and the environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Wildlife of Burkina Faso">Wildlife of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>Burkina Faso has a larger number of elephants than many countries in West Africa. Lions, leopards and buffalo can also be found here, including the dwarf or red buffalo, a smaller reddish-brown animal which looks like a fierce kind of short-legged cow. Other large predators live in Burkina Faso, such as the cheetah, the caracal or African lynx, the spotted hyena and the African wild dog, one of the continent’s most endangered species.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Burkina Faso's <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Wildlife in Burkina Faso" class="mw-redirect">fauna and flora</a> are protected in four national parks:</p>
<ul>
<li>The W National Park in the east which passes Burkina Faso, Benin, and Niger</li>
<li>The Arly Wildlife Reserve (Arly National Park in the east)</li>
<li>The Léraba -Comoé Classified Forest and Partial Reserve of Wildlife in the west</li>
<li>The Mare aux Hippopotames in the west</li>
</ul>
<p>and several reserves: see <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Africa" title="List of national parks in Africa">List of national parks in Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserves_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Nature reserves of Burkina Faso" class="mw-redirect">Nature reserves of Burkina Faso</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Economy of Burkina Faso">Economy of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="864" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burkina Faso's exports in 2009. Every year gold and cotton constitute more than 70% of the country's exports and the prices of these commodities have fluctuated significantly in the past 10 years.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The value of Burkina Faso's exports fell from $2.77 billion in 2011 to $754 million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Agriculture represents 32% of its gross domestic product and occupies 80% of the working population. It consists mostly of rearing livestock. Especially in the south and southwest, the people grow crops of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_millet" title="Pearl millet">pearl millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize (corn)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, rice and cotton, with surpluses to be sold. A large part of the economic activity of the country is funded by international aid.</p>
<p>Burkina Faso was ranked the 111th safest investment destination in the world in the March 2011 Euromoney Country Risk rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">Remittances</a> used to be an important source of income to Burkina Faso until the 1990s, when unrest in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire" class="mw-redirect">Côte d'Ivoire</a>, the main destination for Burkinabe emigrants, forced many to return home. Remittances now account for less than 1% of GDP.</p>
<p>Burkina Faso is part of the <a href="/wiki/West_African_Monetary_and_Economic_Union" title="West African Monetary and Economic Union" class="mw-redirect">West African Monetary and Economic Union</a> (UMEOA) and has adopted the <a href="/wiki/CFA_Franc" title="CFA Franc" class="mw-redirect">CFA Franc</a>. This is issued by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_West_African_States" title="Central Bank of the West African States" class="mw-redirect">Central Bank of the West African States</a> (BCEAO), situated in <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>, Senegal. The BCEAO manages the monetary and reserve policy of the member states, and provides regulation and oversight of financial sector and banking activity. A legal framework regarding licensing, bank activities, organizational and capital requirements, inspections and sanctions (all applicable to all countries of the Union) is in place, having been reformed significantly in 1999. <a href="/wiki/Micro-finance" title="Micro-finance" class="mw-redirect">Micro-finance</a> institutions are governed by a separate law, which regulates micro-finance activities in all WAEMU countries. The insurance sector is regulated through the Inter-African Conference on Insurance Markets (CIMA).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Processing facilities at the Essakane <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">Mine</a> in Burkina Faso.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is mining of copper, iron, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, gold, <a href="/wiki/Cassiterite" title="Cassiterite">cassiterite</a> (tin ore), and phosphates.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> These operations provide employment and generate international aid. In some cases, hospitals maintained by mining companies are available for use by local populations. Gold production increased 32% in 2011 at six gold mine sites, making Burkina Faso the fourth-largest gold producer in Africa, after South Africa, Mali and Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Burkina Faso also hosts the International Art and Craft Fair, Ouagadougou. It is better known by its French name as <a href="/wiki/SIAO" title="SIAO" class="mw-redirect">SIAO</a>, <i>Le Salon International de l' Artisanat de Ouagadougou</i>, and is one of the most important African handicraft fairs.</p>
<p>Burkina Faso is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/220px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/330px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/440px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3556" data-file-height="2667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Grand marché</i> in <a href="/wiki/Koudougou" title="Koudougou">Koudougou</a>, Burkina Faso.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">services</a> remain underdeveloped, the National Office for Water and Sanitation (ONEA), a <a href="/wiki/State-owned" title="State-owned" class="mw-redirect">state-owned</a> <a href="/wiki/Utility_company" title="Utility company" class="mw-redirect">utility company</a> run along commercial lines, is emerging as one of the best-performing utility companies in Africa, .<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> High levels of autonomy and a skilled and dedicated management has driven ONEA's ability to improve production of and access to clean water.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2000, nearly 2 million more people have access to water in the four principal urban centres in the country; the company has kept the quality of <a href="/wiki/Water_infrastructure" title="Water infrastructure" class="mw-redirect">infrastructure</a> high (less than 18% of the water is lost through leaks&#160;– one of the lowest in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>), improved financial reporting, and increased its annual revenue by an average of 12% (well above inflation).<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Challenges remain, including difficulties among some customers in paying for services, with the need to rely on international aid to expand its infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The state-owned, commercially run venture has helped the nation reach its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" title="Millennium Development Goal" class="mw-redirect">Millennium Development Goal</a> (MDG) targets in water-related areas, and has grown as a viable company.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_52-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The growth rate in Burkina Faso is high although it continues to be plagued by corruption and incursions from terrorist groups from Mali and Niger.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The railway station in <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso" title="Bobo Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect">Bobo Dioulasso</a> was built during the colonial era and remains in operation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Transport in Burkina Faso">Transport in Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>Transport in Burkina Faso is hampered by a largely underdeveloped infrastructure.</p>
<p>The main airport is at <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou_Airport" title="Ouagadougou Airport">Ouagadougou</a> and as of June 2014 it had regularly scheduled flights to many destinations in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. There is another international airport at <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso_Airport" title="Bobo Dioulasso Airport">Bobo Dioulasso</a> which has flights to Ouagadougou and <a href="/wiki/Port_Bouet_Airport" title="Port Bouet Airport">Abidjan</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Rail transport in Burkina Faso">Rail transport in Burkina Faso</a> consists of a single line which runs from <a href="/wiki/Kaya,_Burkina_Faso" title="Kaya, Burkina Faso">Kaya</a> to <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a> in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire" class="mw-redirect">Côte d'Ivoire</a> via <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koudougou" title="Koudougou">Koudougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso" title="Bobo Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect">Bobo Dioulasso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banfora" title="Banfora">Banfora</a>. <i>Sitarail</i> operates a passenger train three times a week along the route.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There are 12,506 kilometres of <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highway</a> in Burkina Faso, of which 2,001 kilometres are paved.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouagadougou_(3839513403).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/200px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/300px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/400px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouagadougou_(3839513403).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Burkinabe <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> man in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Demographics of Burkina Faso">Demographics of Burkina Faso</a></div>
<p>Burkina Faso is an ethnically integrated, secular state. Most of Burkina's people are concentrated in the south and center of the country, where their density sometimes exceeds 48 per square kilometer (125/sq. mi.). Hundreds of thousands of Burkinabe migrate regularly to Côte d'Ivoire and Ghana, mainly for seasonal agricultural work. These flows of workers are affected by external events; the September 2002 coup attempt in Côte d'Ivoire and the ensuing fighting meant that hundreds of thousands of Burkinabe returned to Burkina Faso. The regional economy suffered when they were unable to work.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Burkina Faso is 5.93 children born per woman (2014 estimates), the sixth highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
